## 🎓 TEACHING RULES — HOW TO EXPLAIN THINGS

These rules are **non-negotiable**. Every code response MUST follow them.

### Rule T1 — Explain Before Code
Before showing ANY new Kotlin/Python/Bash code that uses a concept the developer hasn't seen before:
- Write a plain-English explanation (2-4 sentences) of WHAT the concept is
- Write a simple real-life analogy (e.g., "Hilt is like a restaurant kitchen that prepares ingredients before a chef needs them — so the chef (ViewModel) doesn't have to go shopping himself")
- THEN show the code

### Rule T2 — Line-by-Line Comments (MANDATORY)
**Every single line of code you write MUST have a comment explaining what it does.**
This rule applies to:
- Kotlin Android code
- Python server/scraping code
- Bash/shell scripts
- Docker Compose YAML
- Gradle build files
- XML files (if any)
- JSON config files

**Comment style:**
```kotlin
// ✅ CORRECT — beginner-friendly comment style
val micButton = remember { mutableStateOf(false) }
// ^ 'remember' keeps this value alive across Compose redraws (like a sticky note on the screen)
// ^ 'mutableStateOf(false)' creates a true/false value that starts as 'false' (mic is OFF)
// ^ When this value changes, Jetpack Compose automatically redraws the mic button
```

```python
# ✅ CORRECT — Python comment style
qdrant_client = QdrantClient(host="localhost", port=6333)
# ^ QdrantClient is the Python library that lets us talk to the Qdrant vector database
# ^ host="localhost" means Qdrant is running on the same machine as this Python script
# ^ port=6333 is the door number (port) that Qdrant listens on — like a phone extension
```

```yaml
# ✅ CORRECT — Docker Compose comment style
services:          # 'services' lists all the programs (containers) we want to run
  fastapi:         # This is our main Python web server — handles all Android app requests
    image: python:3.11-slim   # Use Python 3.11 slim (small) Docker image as the base
    ports:
      - "8000:8000"  # Map port 8000 on Ubuntu to port 8000 inside the container
                     # Format: "HOST_PORT:CONTAINER_PORT"
                     # Android app sends requests to Ubuntu:8000 → reaches FastAPI inside Docker
```

### Rule T3 — Teach File Placement
Whenever you create a new file, always state:
- What folder it goes in
- Why it goes there
- How it relates to other files already created

Example:
```
📁 File: app/src/main/java/com/rushdululilm/app/ui/screens/HomeScreen.kt
   Why here: Android Studio looks for UI screens in the 'ui/screens/' folder by convention.
             'com.rushdululilm.app' matches the package name we set in build.gradle.
   Relates to: MainActivity.kt (which calls this screen), NavGraph.kt (which routes to it)
```

### Rule T4 — Show the Full Picture First
Before writing code for any new feature:
1. Show a simple diagram (ASCII or text) of how the feature connects to other parts
2. List ALL files that will be created or modified
3. Estimate how long it will take to understand and implement
4. Then write the code file by file, top to bottom

## 🚫 ANTI-HALLUCINATION RULES — ABSOLUTE PROHIBITIONS

These rules exist to protect the integrity of Islamic knowledge and the developer's time.

### Rule AH1 — NEVER Invent Islamic Rulings
```
❌ STRICTLY FORBIDDEN: Writing or suggesting any Islamic fatwa, ruling, hadith reference,
   or Quranic interpretation from your own LLM knowledge.

✅ CORRECT BEHAVIOUR: Every Islamic answer in app code must come from the RAG pipeline.
   The RAG prompt MUST always include:
   "Answer ONLY from the provided context. Do NOT use your own knowledge.
    If the answer is not in the provided context, say: 'I could not find an answer
    in the approved Islamic sources. Please consult a qualified scholar.'
    Always cite the exact source URL at the end of your answer."
```

### Rule AH2 — NEVER Hallucinate Library Versions or APIs
```
❌ FORBIDDEN: Making up function names, parameters, or API methods for libraries.
✅ REQUIRED: If unsure about an exact API, say:
   "I am not 100% certain of this API signature. Please verify this in the official docs at [URL]."
   Then show the APPROXIMATE code with a comment: // ⚠️ VERIFY THIS API IN DOCS BEFORE RUNNING
```

### Rule AH3 — NEVER Skip the Three-Tier Offline Fallback
```
❌ FORBIDDEN: Implementing any feature that only works with internet — no offline fallback.
✅ REQUIRED: Every feature that needs the internet MUST have all three tiers:
   Tier 1 → Internet (server via cloud/VPS)
   Tier 2 → LAN (server via local Wi-Fi 192.168.x.x)
   Tier 3 → Fully offline (on-device — Room DB, whisper.cpp JNI, Opus-MT ONNX, Android TTS)
```

### Rule AH4 — NEVER Exceed Hardware Limits
```
Developer's GPU: NVIDIA GTX 1650ti — 4GB VRAM ONLY
❌ FORBIDDEN: Suggesting any AI model that needs more than 3.5GB VRAM
✅ ALLOWED models (verified to fit in 4GB VRAM):
   - Qwen3:4b Q4_K_M (2.5GB VRAM) — LLM
   - faster-whisper-large-v3-turbo INT8 (1.5GB VRAM) — STT
   - paraphrase-multilingual-mpnet-base-v2 (CPU, ~420MB RAM) — embeddings
   - IndicTrans2 indic-en-1B (fits in 3GB VRAM with INT8) — translation
   - Coqui XTTS-v2 (fits in 3GB VRAM) — TTS
   If multiple GPU services run together → warn developer to start them one at a time.
```

### Rule AH5 — NEVER Add Telemetry or Third-Party Analytics
```
❌ STRICTLY FORBIDDEN: Adding any of these to the Android app or backend:
   - Google Analytics / Firebase Analytics
   - Google Crashlytics
   - Facebook SDK
   - Any third-party crash reporter or event tracker
   - Any cloud LLM API calls (OpenAI, Anthropic API, Google Gemini API) — ALL inference is local

✅ ONLY ALLOWED tracking: Local app usage stats stored in Room DB on the user's phone only.
```

### Rule AH6 — NEVER Change the Package Name
```
Android package name is fixed: com.rushdululilm.app
❌ FORBIDDEN: Suggesting any other package name — this breaks Play Store listing.
```

### Rule AH7 — Source URL is MANDATORY in Every Answer
```
❌ FORBIDDEN: Showing a fatwa answer in the app without the source URL.
✅ REQUIRED: Every answer displayed must show:
   - The answer text (in user's language)
   - "Source: [clickable URL]" below the answer
   - If multiple sources: list all of them
```

## 🏗️ PROJECT ARCHITECTURE QUICK REFERENCE

```
App Name:        Rushd-ul-Ilm (رشد العلم — Growth of Knowledge)
Package:         com.rushdululilm.app
Language:        Kotlin 2.x (Android) + Python 3.11 (backend)
Android UI:      Jetpack Compose (NO XML layouts)
Architecture:    MVVM + StateFlow + Hilt DI
Local DB:        Room (SQLite wrapper) with FTS5 for offline search
HTTP:            Retrofit + OkHttp → FastAPI server
Video:           ExoPlayer / Media3
Audio capture:   AudioRecord API at 16kHz mono PCM
Offline STT:     whisper.cpp via Android NDK + JNI (ggml-small-q5_0, 182MB)
Offline Trans:   Opus-MT ONNX INT8 via ONNX Runtime Android (~525MB total)
Offline TTS:     Android TextToSpeech API + Google Telugu/Urdu voice packs
Network check:   ConnectivityManager + OkHttp socket ping (200ms timeout)

Server (Ubuntu — GTX 1650ti):
  FastAPI:        port 8000  — main API server
  Ollama:         port 11434 — serves Qwen3:4b Q4_K_M locally
  Qdrant:         port 6333  — vector DB for semantic search
  IndicTrans2:    port 8001  — Telugu/Urdu ↔ English translation
  Coqui XTTS-v2: port 8002  — TTS in Telugu, Urdu, Arabic, English
  faster-whisper: port 8003  — GPU speech-to-text
  Neo4j (Graphiti): ports 7474/7687 — knowledge graph memory
  Mem0:           port 8100  — cross-session agent memory

Islamic Sources (APPROVED — do not add others without developer permission):
  1. https://islamqa.info/en      (Neutral — no madhab)
  2. https://islamqa.org          (Neutral — no madhab)
  3. https://darulifta-deoband.com/en  (Hanafi madhab)
  4. Custom sources (PDFs, Obsidian .md, offline HTML — user-configurable)

Offline data paths on developer's Ubuntu machine:
  islamqa.info:  /home/hidayat/Documents/Islamic Knowledge Q&A App/islamqa.info-offline/
  deoband:       /home/hidayat/Documents/Islamic Knowledge Q&A App/darulifta-deoband.com-offline/
  Videos:        /home/hidayat/Documents/Islamic YouTube Video Database/

Developer machine OS: Parrot OS Linux (primary), Windows (secondary, dual-boot)
```

## 📱 UI/UX RULES FOR ILLITERATE USERS — NEVER VIOLATE THESE

```
1. Mic button MUST cover at least 40% of the home screen height — it is the primary action
2. All button labels in BOTH Telugu AND English — never English only
3. Minimum touch target: 48dp for ALL interactive elements
4. Minimum font size: 16sp for ALL user-facing text — never smaller
5. Color coding:
   - Green (#2E7D32) → Islamic/Halal answers, positive guidance
   - Calm blue (#1565C0) → Quranic references
   - Orange (#E65100) → Offline mode indicator (always visible when no internet)
   - Red (#B71C1C) → Errors only
6. 'Read Aloud' button MUST always be visible on answer screen — NEVER hidden in a menu
7. Offline mode MUST show a banner: "📵 Offline Mode — Using Downloaded Knowledge"
8. Answer text in user's language (Telugu/Urdu) is ALWAYS larger than source URL text
9. Loading indicators: always show a spinner with text like "Searching Islamic sources..."
10. No technical error messages to the user — translate them:
    e.g., "HTTP 503" → "Server is busy. Please try again in a moment."
```

## ⚡ QUICK DECISION RULES

| Question | Answer |
|----------|--------|
| Which LLM for answers? | Qwen3:4b via Ollama — always local, never cloud |
| Which embedding model? | paraphrase-multilingual-mpnet-base-v2 |
| Which vector DB? | Qdrant (self-hosted Docker) |
| Which RAG framework? | LlamaIndex |
| Which translation? | IndicTrans2 (online) / Opus-MT ONNX (offline) |
| Which STT? | faster-whisper-turbo (online) / whisper.cpp JNI (offline) |
| Which TTS? | Coqui XTTS-v2 (online) / Android TTS API (offline) |
| New Islamic source? | Ask developer for permission first — do NOT add automatically |
| Cloud LLM API? | NEVER — all inference is local on GTX 1650ti |
| Firebase? | NEVER — no Google telemetry |
| New feature without offline fallback? | REFUSE — implement all three tiers or ask how to |

## graphify

This project has a knowledge graph at graphify-out/ with god nodes, community structure, and cross-file relationships.

Rules:
- For codebase questions, first run `graphify query "<question>"` when graphify-out/graph.json exists. Use `graphify path "<A>" "<B>"` for relationships and `graphify explain "<concept>"` for focused concepts. These return a scoped subgraph, usually much smaller than GRAPH_REPORT.md or raw grep output.
- If graphify-out/wiki/index.md exists, use it for broad navigation instead of raw source browsing.
- Read graphify-out/GRAPH_REPORT.md only for broad architecture review or when query/path/explain do not surface enough context.
- After modifying code, run `graphify update .` to keep the graph current (AST-only, no API cost).

    ← System prompt for all AI agents\n│\n├── activity-logs/\n│   └── ACTIVITY_LOG.md                 ← Session log — read this second\n│\n├── Report Documentation/               ← Detailed docs for LlamaIndex + Qdrant + Ollama\n│   ├── stt_service.py                  ← faster-whisper endpoint\n│   ├── translation_service.py          ← IndicTrans2 endpoint\n│   └── tts_service.py                  ← Coqui XTTS-v2 endpoint\n│\n├── scraping/                           ← Islamic source download scripts\n│   ├── fast_mirror.py                  ← islamqa.info scraper (EXISTS)\n│   ├── dump_to_db.py                   ← islamqa.info → SQLite (EXISTS)\n│   └── deoband_offline_downloader.py   ← Deoband scraper (EXISTS)\n│\n└── video-database/                     ← Islamic lecture indexing scripts\n    ├── index_videos.py                 ← FFmpeg metadata extraction\n    └── transcribe_videos.py            ← faster-whisper batch transcription\n```\n\n---\n\n## 🔁 THREE-TIER OFFLINE FALLBACK — MANDATORY FOR ALL FEATURES\n\nEvery feature that touches the internet MUST implement all three tiers.\nThe app switches tiers automatically using ConnectivityManager + socket ping.\n\n```\nTier 1 — Internet available:\n  STT:         faster-whisper-large-v3-turbo GPU (port 8003) — ~1 second\n  Translation: IndicTrans2 GPU (port 8001) — best accuracy\n  TTS:         Coqui XTTS-v2 (port 8002) — natural voice\n  Q&A:         LlamaIndex + Qdrant semantic + Qwen3:4b (ports 6333, 11434)\n  Video search: Qdrant transcript search\n\nTier 2 — LAN only (same Wi-Fi as Ubuntu machine):\n  All same as Tier 1 but via 192.168.x.x instead of cloud IP\n\nTier 3 — Fully offline (no network at all):\n  STT:         whisper.cpp JNI (ggml-small-q5_0, 182MB, on-device) — ~8 sec\n  Translation: Opus-MT ONNX INT8 (on-device, ~525MB total)\n  TTS:         Android TextToSpeech API + Google voice packs (~50MB)\n  Q&A:         Room FTS5 keyword search on downloaded SQLite fatwa DB\n  Video search: Room FTS5 on downloaded video metadata SQLite DB\n  Video play:  ExoPlayer from local phone storage\n```\n\n**Network detection code (use this exact pattern):**\n```kotlin\n// Check network tier in this order — always check LAN before internet\nfun detectNetworkTier(context: Context): NetworkTier {\n    val cm = context.getSystemService(Context.CONNECTIVITY_SERVICE) as ConnectivityManager\n    // Check if ANY network is available at all\n    val network = cm.activeNetwork ?: return NetworkTier.OFFLINE\n    val caps = cm.getNetworkCapabilities(network) ?: return NetworkTier.OFFLINE\n    // Try to ping the local Ubuntu server (LAN check — 200ms timeout)\n    return if (pingServer(\"192.168.1.100\", 8000, timeoutMs = 200)) {\n        NetworkTier.LAN  // Local server is reachable\n    } else if (caps.hasCapability(NetworkCapabilities.NET_CAPABILITY_INTERNET)) {\n        NetworkTier.INTERNET  // Internet is available, use cloud/VPS\n    } else {\n        NetworkTier.OFFLINE  // No network at all — use on-device models\n    }\n}\n\nenum class NetworkTier { INTERNET, LAN, OFFLINE }\n```\n\n---\n\n## 🎨 UI RULES (For Illiterate Users — NEVER VIOLATE)\n\n```\n1. Mic button: minimum 40% of screen height — it is the PRIMARY action\n2. All labels: Telugu AND English — never English only\n3. Touch targets: minimum 48dp for every button/interactive element\n4. Font sizes: minimum 16sp for all user-facing text — no exceptions\n5. Colors:\n   - #2E7D32 (dark green) → Islamic answers, halal guidance\n   - #1565C0 (calm blue) → Quranic references\n   - #E65100 (orange) → Offline mode indicator banner\n   - #B71C1C (red) → Errors only\n6. \"Read Aloud\" button: ALWAYS visible on answer screen, minimum 56dp height\n7. Offline banner: show at TOP of screen when Tier 3 is active:\n   \"📵 Offline Mode — Using Downloaded Knowledge\"\n8. Loading: always show progress with friendly text (\"Searching Islamic sources...\")\n9. Error messages: translate to human-readable Telugu/Urdu — no HTTP codes to users\n10. Answer layout: answer text → source name → [clickable source URL] → Read Aloud button\n```\n\n---\n\n## 📝 CODE QUALITY RULES\n\n```\nRULE C1: Every code file begins with a header comment block:\n         // File: [filename]\n         // Purpose: [what this file does in one sentence]\n         // Layer: [which of the 6 layers this belongs to]\n         // Depends on: [other files this imports from]\n         // Created: [date] | Modified: [date]\n         // Developer: Shaik Hidayatullah\n\nRULE C2: Every function has a docstring/KDoc comment explaining:\n         - What it does\n         - What each parameter means\n         - What it returns\n         - Any important edge cases\n\nRULE C3: Every line of code has an inline comment (see Teaching Rule T2)\n\nRULE C4: No magic numbers — every number is a named constant:\n         ❌ Thread.sleep(200)\n         ✅ val LAN_PING_TIMEOUT_MS = 200L; Thread.sleep(LAN_PING_TIMEOUT_MS)\n\nRULE C5: All strings shown to users come from strings.xml (Android) — never hardcoded\n\nRULE C6: All sensitive values (server IPs, API keys if any) go in local.properties\n         or environment variables — NEVER hardcoded in source code\n\nRULE C7: Error handling on every network call — no silent failures\n```\n\n---\n\n## 🏃 SPRINT SYSTEM RULES — HOW TO EXECUTE TASKS\n\nThese rules govern how every AI agent breaks down and executes work. Read SPRINT_SYSTEM.md for the full micro-task breakdown.\n\n```\nRULE S1 — ONE MICRO-TASK PER RESPONSE\n  Do exactly one micro-task per response. Never combine two micro-tasks.\n  If the current micro-task finishes in under 5 minutes, proceed to the next\n  one in the same session. If it takes over 40 minutes and is not done, STOP,\n  split it into sub-tasks (MT3a, MT3b), document where you stopped,\n  and update ACTIVITY_LOG.md with the partial completion.\n\nRULE S2 — STATE THE MICRO-TASK ID FIRST\n  Every response that does coding work begins with:\n  \"Starting micro-task [ID]: [one-sentence description from SPRINT_SYSTEM.md]\"\n  This lets the developer know exactly where in the plan we are.\n\nRULE S3 — VERIFY DONE CONDITION BEFORE DECLARING COMPLETE\n  Every micro-task in SPRINT_SYSTEM.md has a DONE CONDITION block.\n  Read it. Verify every item in it is met before saying the task is complete.\n  If a DONE CONDITION item fails — fix it before moving on. Never skip it.\n\nRULE S4 — ASK BEFORE ADVANCING TO NEXT SPRINT\n  You may advance automatically between micro-tasks within the same sub-sprint.\n  But before starting a NEW sprint (e.g., moving from Sprint 1.2 to Sprint 1.3),\n  stop and tell the developer:\n  \"Sprint [X.Y] is complete. All DONE CONDITIONS verified.\n   Ready to begin Sprint [X.Y+1]: [sprint goal].\n   First micro-task will be [ID]. Shall I continue?\"\n  Wait for confirmation before starting the new sprint.\n\nRULE S5 — NEVER SKIP A MICRO-TASK\n  Every micro-task exists for a reason. Never say \"this one is obvious, I'll skip it.\"\n  If a micro-task seems trivial, complete it quickly and document it.\n  Skipped tasks create hidden gaps that cause failures in later phases.\n\nRULE S6 — TEACH BEFORE CODE, EVERY TIME\n  For every new concept introduced by a micro-task (a new Kotlin keyword,\n  a new Android Studio panel, a new Gradle concept), write:\n    - What it is in plain English (2-4 sentences)\n    - A real-life analogy\n    - THEN the code with every line commented\n  The developer is a beginner. Open terminal\n  2. Check if KVM is already enabled: ls /dev/kvm\n     - If you see /dev/kvm → KVM is ready, skip to step 5\n     - If \"No such file\" → continue to step 3\n  3. Gson converter — converts JSON responses to Kotlin data classes\n  - ExoPlayer / Media3 — video player\n  - Navigation Compose — handles navigation between screens\n  - Coroutines — for async operations (network calls, database)\n  - WorkManager — background sync of offline databases\n  - ONNX Runtime Android 1.17.3 — runs Opus-MT offline translation on phone\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  Gradle syncs without errors after saving the file.\n  \"BUILD SUCCESSFUL\" shown in the Build tab.\n  No red squiggly lines in build.gradle.kts.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P1.S1.SS2.MT3\n```\n\n##### Micro-task P1.S1.SS2.MT3 — Configure Hilt in Application Class\n```\nTASK:   Set up Hilt Dependency Injection — create the Application class\n\nWHY HILT EXISTS (explain this before any code):\n  In Android, many classes need the same objects — for example, every screen\n  might need the database, the network client, and the ViewModel.\n  Without Hilt, you'd have to manually create and pass these objects everywhere.\n  Hilt is like a smart factory — you tell it what objects exist once,\n  and it automatically provides them wherever they're needed.\n  This is called \"Dependency Injection\" (DI).\n\nFILES TO CREATE:\n  1. android-app/app/src/main/java/com/rushdululilm/app/RushdulIlmApplication.kt\n     - Add @HiltAndroidApp annotation on the Application class\n     - Explain what @HiltAndroidApp does in a comment\n\n  2. Modify AndroidManifest.xml:\n     - Add android:name=\".RushdulIlmApplication\" to the <application> tag\n     - Explain why this is needed in a comment\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  The app compiles without errors.\n  Run the app on emulator — it should show a blank \"Hello Android\" screen.\n  No Hilt-related errors in Logcat.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P1.S1.SS2.MT4 (run app for first time)\n```\n\n##### Micro-task P1.S1.SS2.MT4 — Run the App for the First Time\n```\nTASK:   Run the app on the emulator to verify the project setup is correct\n\nSTEP BY STEP:\n  1. In Android Studio, at the top toolbar: make sure the emulator is selected\n     (dropdown shows \"Pixel_5_API_31\" or similar)\n  2. Click the green ▶ Run button (or press Shift+F10)\n  3. Wait for the build to complete (progress at bottom)\n  4. The emulator should open the app and show a screen with \"Hello Android!\" text\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  App runs on the emulator without crashing.\n  \"Hello Android!\" (or similar default Compose text) is visible on screen.\n  Logcat (bottom panel) shows no ERROR or FATAL lines.\n\nSPRINT 1.1 IS COMPLETE WHEN THIS MICRO-TASK IS DONE.\nNEXT SPRINT: 1.2 — App Structure & Navigation\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P1.S2.SS1.MT1\n```\n\n---\n\n### SPRINT 1.2 — App Structure & Navigation\n**Goal:** All 4 screens exist as empty placeholders. When you navigate to HomeScreen, you tell\n        the navigation system \"go to the 'home' route\".\n        Putting all route strings in one file prevents typos and makes it easy\n        to change a route name later without hunting through multiple files.\n\nFILE TO CREATE:\n  Path: com/rushdululilm/app/ui/screens/Routes.kt\n\nCONTENT (write with full comments):\n  object Routes {\n      const val HOME = \"home\"           // Main screen with mic button\n      const val ANSWER = \"answer\"       // Shows the fatwa answer + source URL\n      const val VIDEO_LIBRARY = \"video_library\"  // Searchable video list\n      const val SETTINGS = \"settings\"   // App preferences and offline DB download\n  }\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  Routes.kt compiles without errors.\n  All 4 route constants are defined and commented.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P1.S2.SS2.MT1\n```\n\n---\n\n#### Sub-sprint 1.2.2 — Build the Navigation Graph\n\n##### Micro-task P1.S2.SS2.MT1 — Create 4 Empty Placeholder Screens\n```\nTASK:   Create 4 minimal Jetpack Compose screen files — empty placeholders only\n\nWHY JETPACK COMPOSE (explain before any code):\n  Traditional Android used XML files to describe the UI (like HTML for Android).\n  Jetpack Compose is newer and lets you write UI directly in Kotlin code.\n  A @Composable function is a function that draws something on screen.\n  When its data changes, Compose automatically redraws it — like a live webpage.\n\nFILES TO CREATE:\n\n  1. ui/screens/HomeScreen.kt\n     - Create a @Composable function: fun RushdulIlmNavGraph()\n  - Use rememberNavController() to create the navigation controller\n  - Use NavHost with startDestination = Routes.HOME\n  - Add composable() entries for all 4 routes: HOME, ANSWER, VIDEO_LIBRARY, SETTINGS\n  - Each composable() block calls the corresponding screen function\n  - Add a bottom navigation bar with 4 icons:\n    * Home (mic icon)\n    * Video Library (video icon)\n    * Settings (settings icon)\n    * [Answer screen is navigated to programmatically — no bottom nav tab for it]\n  - Every line commented\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  NavGraph.kt compiles without errors.\n  Each route is defined and linked to the correct screen Composable.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P1.S2.SS2.MT3\n```\n\n##### Micro-task P1.S2.SS2.MT3 — Wire NavGraph into MainActivity & Test Navigation\n```\nTASK:   Replace the default MainActivity content with RushdulIlmNavGraph()\n        Then run the app and verify you can navigate between all 4 screens.\n\nFILE TO MODIFY:\n  Path: com/rushdululilm/app/MainActivity.kt\n\nCHANGES:\n  - Model: the data (Islamic answers, language choice)\n  - View: the UI (Composables you can see)\n  - ViewModel: the brain between them — holds state, handles logic\n  Think of it like a restaurant:\n  - The kitchen (Model) has the food (data)\n  - The dining room (View) is what customers see\n  - The waiter (ViewModel) carries orders and food between them\n  The ViewModel survives screen rotations — Composables do not.\n  This means if you rotate your phone, you don't lose the answer being displayed.\n\nFILE TO CREATE:\n  Path: com/rushdululilm/app/viewmodel/HomeViewModel.kt\n\nREQUIREMENTS:\n  - @HiltViewModel annotation on the class\n  - class HomeViewModel @Inject constructor() : ViewModel()\n  - StateFlow properties (with detailed comments):\n    * selectedLanguage: MutableStateFlow<String>(\"Telugu\")\n    * selectedSource: MutableStateFlow<String>(\"all\")\n    * isRecording: MutableStateFlow<Boolean>(false)\n    * uiState: MutableStateFlow<HomeUiState>(HomeUiState.Idle)\n  - Create a sealed class HomeUiState with states:\n    * Idle — waiting for user to press mic\n    * Recording — currently capturing audio\n    * Processing — sending audio to server / on-device model\n    * NavigatingToAnswer(answerId: String) — answer ready, navigate to AnswerScreen\n    * Error(message: String) — something went wrong\n  - Functions (placeholder — no real logic yet):\n    * fun onMicPressed() — toggles isRecording, logs to console\n    * fun onLanguageSelected(language: String)\n    * fun onSourceSelected(source: String)\n  - Explain StateFlow in comments: \"StateFlow is like a live variable —\n    when it changes, every Composable observing it automatically redraws\"\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  HomeViewModel.kt compiles without errors.\n  @HiltViewModel annotation is present.\n  All StateFlow properties are defined with comments.\n  HomeUiState sealed class has all 5 states.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P1.S3.SS1.MT6\n```\n\n##### Micro-task P1.S3.SS1.MT6 — Build the Full HomeScreen Layout\n```\nTASK:   Replace the placeholder HomeScreen with the real UI using components built above\n\nFILE TO MODIFY:\n  Path: com/rushdululilm/app/ui/screens/HomeScreen.kt\n\nLAYOUT STRUCTURE (build this exactly):\n  Scaffold (Material3 Scaffold gives us the app bar and structure)\n  └── Column (vertical layout, fills entire screen)\n      ├── TopAppBar — App name: \"Rushd-ul-Ilm\" + offline status indicator\n      ├── OfflineBanner (shown only when offline) — orange banner at top\n      ├── Spacer (16dp)\n      ├── LanguageSelector (connected to HomeViewModel.selectedLanguage)\n      ├── Spacer (12dp)\n      ├── SourceSelector (connected to HomeViewModel.selectedSource)\n      ├── Spacer (24dp)\n      ├── MicButton — fills remaining 40% of screen\n      │   onClick → homeViewModel.onMicPressed()\n      │   isRecording → homeViewModel.isRecording\n      ├── Spacer (16dp)\n      └── Text — instruction text in Telugu + English:\n               \"మైక్ నొక్కి మీ ప్రశ్న అడగండి\"\n               \"Press mic and ask your question\"\n               Font: 16sp, color = TextPrimary, textAlign = Center\n\nREQUIREMENTS:\n  - Open terminal in Parrot OS\n  2. Uninstall old versions: sudo apt remove docker docker-engine docker.io containerd runc\n  3. Install dependencies: sudo apt update && sudo apt install ca-certificates curl gnupg lsb-release\n  4. Add Docker GPG key: \n     sudo mkdir -p /etc/apt/keyrings\n     curl -fsSL https://download.docker.com/linux/debian/gpg | sudo gpg --dearmor -o /etc/apt/keyrings/docker.gpg\n  5. Set up repository:\n     echo \"deb [arch=$(dpkg --print-architecture) signed-by=/etc/apt/keyrings/docker.gpg] https://download.docker.com/linux/debian $(lsb_release -cs) stable\" | sudo tee /etc/apt/sources.list.d/docker.list > /dev/null\n  6. Install Docker: sudo apt update && sudo apt install docker-ce docker-ce-cli containerd.io docker-compose-plugin\n  7. Start and enable Docker: sudo systemctl enable docker --now\n  8. Add user to docker group: sudo usermod -aG docker $USER (log out and back in to apply)\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  'docker --version' shows a valid version.\n  'docker compose version' shows a valid version.\n  'sudo docker run hello-world' runs successfully.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P2.S1.SS1.MT2\n```\n\n##### Micro-task P2.S1.SS1.MT2 — Install NVIDIA Container Toolkit\n```\nTASK:   Install NVIDIA Container Toolkit so Docker can use the GTX 1650ti GPU\n\nWHY:    Our AI models (Ollama, STT, TTS) need the GPU to run fast.\n        Docker containers are isolated from the host hardware by default.\n        The NVIDIA Container Toolkit is the \"bridge\" that lets a container\n        talk to your NVIDIA GPU.\n\nSTEP BY STEP:\n  1. Add the package repository:\n     curl -fsSL https://nvidia.github.io/libnvidia-container/gpgkey | sudo gpg --dearmor -o /usr/share/keyrings/nvidia-container-toolkit-keyring.gpg \\\n     && curl -s -L https://nvidia.github.io/libnvidia-container/stable/deb/nvidia-container-toolkit.list | \\\n     sed 's#deb https://#deb [signed-by=/usr/share/keyrings/nvidia-container-toolkit-keyring.gpg] https://#g' | \\\n     sudo tee /etc/apt/sources.list.d/nvidia-container-toolkit.list\n  2. Install the toolkit: sudo apt update && sudo apt install nvidia-container-toolkit\n  3. Configure Docker to use the toolkit: sudo nvidia-ctk runtime configure --runtime=docker\n  4. Restart Docker: sudo systemctl restart docker\n  5. Verify GPU access: docker run --rm --runtime=nvidia --gpus all nvidia/cuda:11.8.0-base-ubuntu22.04 nvidia-smi\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  'nvidia-smi' output is visible from within the test Docker container.\n  The output correctly identifies the GTX 1650ti with 4GB VRAM.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P2.S2.SS1.MT1\n```\n\n---\n\n### SPRINT 2.2 — Create docker-compose.yml Skeleton\n\n##### Micro-task P2.S2.SS1.MT1 — Create Base docker-compose.yml\n```\nTASK:   Create the project's main Docker orchestration file\n\nWHY:    Instead of starting 5 different programs manually, Docker Compose\n        lets us start EVERYTHING with one command: 'docker compose up -d'.\n        It handles networking between services and persistent storage.\n\nFILE TO CREATE: backend/docker-compose.yml\n\nREQUIREMENTS:\n  - Define a custom network: 'rushd-network'\n  - Define volumes for data persistence: 'ollama_data', 'qdrant_data'\n  - Include service placeholders (comments only for now)\n  - Every line commented for a beginner\n\nDONE CONDITION:\n  'docker compose config' shows no syntax errors.\n  The backend/ folder exists.\n\nNEXT MICRO-TASK: P2.S3.SS1.MT1\n```\n\n---\n\n### SPRINT 2.3 — Start Ollama + pull Qwen3:4b model\n\n##### Micro-task P2.S3.SS1.MT1 — Configure Ollama Service\n```\nTASK:   Add Ollama to docker-compose.yml and pull the local LLM model\n\nSTEP BY STEP:\n  1. ### Starting micro-task P2.S1.SS1.MT1: Install Docker Engine on Parrot OS Linux

Before we begin the installation, I will explain what **Docker** is and why we need it for Phase 2.

**What is Docker?**
Docker is like a shipping container system for software. In the real world, shipping containers allow any ship to carry any cargo because the container is a standard size. In software, Docker "packages" a program (like our AI models or the FastAPI server) along with everything it needs to run (libraries, Python version, etc.) into a **Container**. This ensures that if it works on my machine, it will work exactly the same on your machine, regardless of the OS version.

**Why do we need it?**
Our project uses multiple complex AI models (Ollama for the LLM, Qdrant for the vector database, faster-whisper for speech-to-text, etc.). Installing these directly on your system can cause "dependency hell" where one program needs one version of a library and another needs a different one. Docker isolates them so they don't fight with each other.

I will now check if Docker is already installed and then proceed with the installation steps if needed.

**Step 1: Check current Docker status**
I will run `docker --version` and `docker compose version` to see if they are already present.

**Step 2: Clean up old versions**
I will remove any old or conflicting versions of Docker to ensure a clean install.

**Step 3: Install Docker Engine**
I will follow the official Debian-based installation (Parrot OS is based on Debian) as outlined in the sprint instructions.

**Step 4: Verify**
I will run the `hello-world` container to confirm everything is working.

---

I'll start by checking the environment and existing installations. Moving to execution.

**Note for the developer:** After I add your user to the `docker` group in Step 8, you will need to log out and log back in (or restart your terminal) for the changes to take effect so you can run docker commands without `sudo`.

```bash
# Checking if Docker is already installed
docker --version || echo "Docker not found"
docker compose version || echo "Docker Compose not found"
```

I will execute these checks now. After checking, I will proceed with the installation steps as defined in `SPRINT_SYSTEM.md`.**Tool Command**:

### Starting micro-task P2.S1.SS1.MT2: Install NVIDIA Container Toolkit

**What is the NVIDIA Container Toolkit?**
Docker containers are isolated "bubbles." By default, they cannot see your computer's hardware, like your NVIDIA GTX 1650ti GPU. The **NVIDIA Container Toolkit** is a specialized tool that acts as a bridge. It allows Docker containers to "reach out" and use the GPU's power for tasks like AI speech-to-text, translation, and local LLM inference.

**Why do we need it?**
Running AI models on a CPU is very slow (like walking). Running them on a GPU is very fast (like flying). For our Islamic Q&A app to feel "snappy" and respond in seconds, we MUST use your GPU.

**Step 1: Check if already installed**
I will check if the NVIDIA toolkit is already present by running a test container that calls `nvidia-smi`.

**Step 2: Installation (if needed)**
If not found, I will follow the steps in `SPRINT_SYSTEM.md` to add the NVIDIA repository and install the toolkit.

**Step 3: Configuration**
I will configure Docker to use the NVIDIA runtime and restart the service.

**Step 4: Verification**
I will run a CUDA container and verify that it can see your GTX 1650ti and its 4GB of VRAM.

---

I'll start by checking if the NVIDIA Container Toolkit is already configured.**Tool Command**:

## MODEL ✨

Your GPU drivers are working perfectly! Interestingly, `nvidia-smi` reports an **RTX 3050** (4GB) rather than the **GTX 1650ti** mentioned in our earlier notes. This is good news, as the RTX 3050 has better AI performance (Tensor cores), though we still have the **4GB VRAM limit** to respect.

I will now install the **NVIDIA Container Toolkit**.

**Step 1 & 2: Add Repository and Install Toolkit**
I will combine these into a single command sequence.

**Step 3 & 4: Configure and Restart Docker**
I will configure the runtime and restart the service so it takes effect.

**Step 5: Verify**
I will run the CUDA container again.

```bash
# Adding the GPG key and repository
curl -fsSL https://nvidia.github.io/libnvidia-container/gpgkey | sudo gpg --dearmor -o /usr/share/keyrings/nvidia-container-toolkit-keyring.gpg \
&& curl -s -L https://nvidia.github.io/libnvidia-container/stable/deb/nvidia-container-toolkit.list | \
sed 's#deb https://#deb [signed-by=/usr/share/keyrings/nvidia-container-toolkit-keyring.gpg] https://#g' | \
sudo tee /etc/apt/sources.list.d/nvidia-container-toolkit.list

# Installing the toolkit
sudo apt update && sudo apt install -y nvidia-container-toolkit

# Configuring Docker
sudo nvidia-ctk runtime configure --runtime=docker

# Restarting Docker
sudo systemctl restart docker
```

I will execute these steps now.**Tool Command**:

## MODEL ✨

I have completed the scheduled tasks for this session.

**Summary of Work:**
1.  **Micro-task P2.S1.SS1.MT1 Complete:** Verified that Docker (v29.5.2) and Docker Compose (v2.40.3) were already installed and that user `hidayat` has the necessary permissions.
2.  **Micro-task P2.S1.SS1.MT2 Complete:** Successfully installed the **NVIDIA Container Toolkit**, configured the Docker runtime, and verified that containers can now access your **RTX 3050** GPU using a CUDA test image.
3.  **Hardware Update:** Detected that the system is running an **RTX 3050 (4GB)** rather than the previously noted GTX 1650ti. I have updated `AGENT_RULES.md` and `GEMINI.md` to reflect this change while maintaining the strict 4GB VRAM safety rules.
4.  **Documentation:** Created the Phase 2 report documentation and updated the sprint progress tracker and activity logs.

**Sprint 2.1 is now 100% complete.**

- **Current Phase:** 2 — Backend Docker Services

## MODEL ✨

**Sprint 2.3 (Micro-task P2.S3.SS1.MT1) is complete!**

I have adapted the setup to perfectly honor your running native instance:

1. **Docker Configuration:** I added the `ollama` service to `docker-compose.yml` and configured it to use the NVIDIA RTX 3050 GPU. 
2. **Model Persistence Hack:** Instead of an isolated Docker volume, I bind-mounted your native `~/.ollama` directory directly into the container (`~/.ollama:/root/.ollama`). This means if you ever decide to run Ollama via Docker, it will *instantly* have access to the `qwen3:4b` model you just downloaded—no 2.5GB re-download required!
3. **Port Collision Prevention:** Because your native `ollama serve` is occupying port 11434, I successfully validated the syntax but **did not** run `docker compose up -d ollama`. This prevents crashing your current setup.

**Current Status:**
- **Current Phase:** 2 — Backend Docker Services
- **Current Sprint:** 2.4 — FastAPI Server Skeleton
- **Next Micro-task:** `P2.S4.SS1.MT1` — Create FastAPI App & Requirements

Shall I proceed with creating the Python backend API (Sprint 2.4)?

---

## USER 🧑‍💻

continue to P2.S4.SS1.MT1

It lists all the external libraries our\n# Python backend needs. When we build the Docker container, Docker will run\n# 'pip install -r requirements.txt' to install them.\n# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n# FastAPI is a modern, fast web framework for building APIs with Python.\n# We use this to create the endpoints the Android app will call.\nfastapi\n\n# Uvicorn is the server that actually runs the FastAPI application.\n# Think of FastAPI as the logic, and Uvicorn as the engine that runs it.\nuvicorn\n\n# Requests is a simple HTTP library. We'll use this inside our FastAPI server\n# to talk to the Ollama server (which runs on a different port/container).\nrequests\n\n# Pydantic is used for data validation. It ensures the data the Android app\n# sends us (like search queries) is in the correct format.\npydantic\n"

## MODEL ✨

**Micro-task P2.S4.SS1.MT1 Complete!**

I have successfully created the foundational Python files for your backend API:
1.  **`backend/requirements.txt`**: This file lists the Python libraries we need (`fastapi` for the API logic, `uvicorn` to run the server, `requests` to talk to Ollama, and `pydantic` for data validation). I added beginner-friendly comments explaining each one.
2.  **`backend/fastapi_server.py`**: I wrote the basic skeleton for the server. It includes the `app` instance and a `/health` endpoint that returns a simple JSON message. Every line is commented to explain what the code is doing.

**Current Status:**
- **Current Phase:** 2 — Backend Docker Services
- **Current Sprint:** 2.4 — FastAPI Server Skeleton
- **Next Micro-task:** `P2.S4.SS1.MT2` — Containerize FastAPI Service (Create the Dockerfile and add it to `docker-compose.yml`).

Shall I proceed to `P2.S4.SS1.MT2` to bundle this Python code into a Docker container and spin it up?

proceed to P2.S4.SS1.MT2

## MODEL ✨

**Tool Command**:
```json
{
  "name": "update_topic",
  "args": {
    "strategic_intent": "Containerizing the FastAPI service by creating a Dockerfile and adding it to the docker-compose orchestration.",
    "summary": "The user requested to proceed to micro-task P2.S4.SS1.MT2. I will create a `Dockerfile` in the `backend/` directory using `python:3.11-slim` as the base image. I will then update `backend/docker-compose.yml` to build this Dockerfile, exposing port 8000. Finally, I will start the FastAPI container using `docker compose up -d fastapi` and verify its liveness via the `/health` endpoint.",
    "title": "Sprint 2.4: Containerize FastAPI Service"
  },
  "id": "update_topic__update_topic_1780405031388_0"
}
```**Tool Command**:
```json
{
  "name": "write_file",
  "args": {
    "file_path": "backend/Dockerfile",
    "content": "# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Rushd-ul-Ilm (رشد العلم) — FastAPI Dockerfile\n# \n# What is this file?\n# A Dockerfile is like a recipe. It tells Docker exactly how to build the \n# \"shipping container\" for our Python API. It starts with a base operating \n# system, copies our code into it, and installs the required libraries.\n# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n# 1. Base Image: Start with a small, lightweight version of Linux that \n# already has Python 3.11 installed. 'slim' means it removes unnecessary files.\nFROM python:3.11-slim\n\n# 2. Working Directory: Create a folder inside the container called /app\n# and make it the current active directory. All following commands run here.\nWORKDIR /app\n\n# 3. Copy Requirements: Copy the requirements.txt file from your host machine\n# into the /app folder inside the container.\nCOPY requirements.txt .\n\n# 4. Install Dependencies: Run 'pip install' inside the container to download\n# and install FastAPI, Uvicorn, Requests, etc. \n# '--no-cache-dir' keeps the container size small by not saving the installers.\nRUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt\n\n# 5. Copy Code: Copy all the rest of our Python code (like fastapi_server.py)\n# from the host machine into the /app folder in the container.\nCOPY . .\n\n# 6. Expose Port: Tell Docker that this container will listen for network \n# traffic on port 8000 (which is the default port for FastAPI).\nEXPOSE 8000\n\n# 7. Start Command: This is the command that runs automatically when the \n# container starts. It tells Uvicorn to run the 'app' variable found inside \n# 'fastapi_server.py'.\n# '--host 0.0.0.0' allows external connections (like from our Android app).\nCMD [\"uvicorn\", \"fastapi_server:app\", \"--host\", \"0.0.0.0\", \"--port\", \"8000\"]\n"
  },
  "id": "write_file__write_file_1780405033335_1"
}
```

---

## USER 🧑‍💻

**Tool Response**:
```json
{
  "id": "update_topic__update_topic_1780405031388_0",
  "name": "update_topic",
  "response": {
    "output": "Current topic: \"Sprint 2.4: Containerize FastAPI Service\"\nTopic summary: The user requested to proceed to micro-task P2.S4.SS1.MT2. I will create a `Dockerfile` in the `backend/` directory using `python:3.11-slim` as the base image. I will then update `backend/docker-compose.yml` to build this Dockerfile, exposing port 8000. Finally, I will start the FastAPI container using `docker compose up -d fastapi` and verify its liveness via the `/health` endpoint.\n\nStrategic Intent: Containerizing the FastAPI service by creating a Dockerfile and adding it to the docker-compose orchestration."
  }
}
```**Tool Response**:

    "output": "Successfully created and wrote to new file: /home/hidayat/Documents/Islamic-Knowledge-Q&A-App/backend/Dockerfile. Here is the updated code:\n# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n# Rushd-ul-Ilm (رشد العلم) — FastAPI Dockerfile\n# \n# What is this file?\n# A Dockerfile is like a recipe. It tells Docker exactly how to build the \n# \"shipping container\" for our Python API. It starts with a base operating \n# system, copies our code into it, and installs the required libraries.\n# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------\n\n# 1. Base Image: Start with a small, lightweight version of Linux that \n# already has Python 3.11 installed. 'slim' means it removes unnecessary files.\nFROM python:3.11-slim\n\n# 2. Working Directory: Create a folder inside the container called /app\n# and make it the current active directory. All following commands run here.\nWORKDIR /app\n\n# 3. Copy Requirements: Copy the requirements.txt file from your host machine\n# into the /app folder inside the container.\nCOPY requirements.txt .\n\n# 4. Install Dependencies: Run 'pip install' inside the container to download\n# and install FastAPI, Uvicorn, Requests, etc. \n# '--no-cache-dir' keeps the container size small by not saving the installers.\nRUN pip install --no-cache-dir -r requirements.txt\n\n# 5. Copy Code: Copy all the rest of our Python code (like fastapi_server.py)\n# from the host machine into the /app folder in the container.\nCOPY . .\n\n# 6. Expose Port: Tell Docker that this container will listen for network \n# traffic on port 8000 (which is the default port for FastAPI).\nEXPOSE 8000\n\n# 7. Start Command: This is the command that runs automatically when the \n# container starts. It tells Uvicorn to run the 'app' variable found inside \n# 'fastapi_server.py'.\n# '--host 0.0.0.0' allows external connections (like from our Android app).\nCMD [\"uvicorn\", \"fastapi_server:app\", \"--host\", \"0.0.0.0\", \"--port\", \"8000\"]\n"
  }
}

## MODEL ✨

**Sprint 2.4 is 100% complete!**

I have successfully containerized your Python API. 

Here is what I accomplished:
1.  **Created a `Dockerfile`:** This file acts as the build recipe for the FastAPI server, pulling a lightweight Python 3.11 image and installing the dependencies from `requirements.txt`. I added detailed comments to explain each step (FROM, WORKDIR, COPY, RUN, CMD).
2.  **Updated `docker-compose.yml`:** I added the `fastapi` service. Importantly, I mounted the local `backend/` folder directly into the container and configured Uvicorn to run with `--reload`. This means you can edit `fastapi_server.py` in your code editor, and the server will instantly restart to reflect your changes without needing to rebuild the Docker image!
3.  **Built and Verified:** I built the image and started the container (`rushd_fastapi`). I then sent a test request to `http://localhost:8000/health` and successfully received the healthy JSON response.

**Current Status:**
- **Current Phase:** 2 — Backend Docker Services
- **Current Sprint:** 2.5 — Qdrant Vector DB Setup
- **Next Micro-task:** `P2.S5.SS1.MT1` — Configure Qdrant Service (Add Qdrant vector database to `docker-compose.yml`).

Shall I proceed to Sprint 2.5 to set up the Qdrant Vector Database?

## MODEL ✨

**Sprint 2.5 is 100% complete!**

I have successfully added and started the **Qdrant Vector Database**.

Here is what I accomplished:
1.  **Updated `docker-compose.yml`:** Added the `qdrant` service.
2.  **Configured Networking & Storage:** I exposed ports 6333 (for the API and Web UI) and 6334 (for high-speed gRPC communication). I also attached the `qdrant_data` permanent volume so your embedded fatwas won't be lost when the container stops.
3.  **Verification:** I started the container and ran a test ping to `http://localhost:6333/`. The database responded instantly with its version information.

**Current Status:**
- **Current Phase:** 2 — Backend Docker Services
- **Current Sprint:** 2.6 — Wire FastAPI to Ollama
